    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1572959815?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008117474" href="/book/show/25985881-ship-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Fantasy, Hobb</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572959815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17954556552628871136">Reading Ship of Destiny fulfilled the majority of my expectations. Being the third and final book of the Liveship Traders trilogy, I was hoping it would do just that. Actually, Ship of Destiny exceeded some of my hopes with an open-ended finish. Matching the standards of the first two books can be no easy task for Robin Hobb, but it’s something I’ve learned not to fear. She always comes through. Somehow the tension provided in these three books only managed to increase as the story continued, wh</span>
  <span id="freeText17954556552628871136" style="display:none">Reading Ship of Destiny fulfilled the majority of my expectations. Being the third and final book of the Liveship Traders trilogy, I was hoping it would do just that. Actually, Ship of Destiny exceeded some of my hopes with an open-ended finish. Matching the standards of the first two books can be no easy task for Robin Hobb, but it’s something I’ve learned not to fear. She always comes through. Somehow the tension provided in these three books only managed to increase as the story continued, which blows my mind. In total truth, many chapters were on the wordy side, but I after completing the series, I realize that I would rather have the whole than only chosen parts.<br /><br />It’s also a pleasing close to the series because it left me with both the feeling of being complete and yet hungry for more. That brings to mind another great point about the author. She is always looking forward in her books, or it seems that way. A trilogy makes up one complete story, but it also provides a tangent to separate story just down the road. If I hadn’t read this series, I would have missed a very satisfying connection to the Rain Wild Chronicles.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17954556552628871136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188179269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7571545817917440774">My brain is too fried to think, and a picture is worth a thousand words so..<br/><br/>Let me open up by showing an accurate depiction of Robin Hobb and her characters..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921740ra/24556556.gif' width='500' height='210' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Yep looks accurate enough to me.. and I thought she was mean to my babies in Farseer :') This series was borderline sadist towards those precious children.. Shall we continue?<br/><br/>When we finally learned the full extent of the flashbacks despite all the previous not-so-subtle hints..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556503.gif' width='317' height='174' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>when THAT scene happened..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556504.gif' width='410' height='203' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>All the other near-hits..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556505.gif' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Then there i</span>
  <span id="freeText7571545817917440774" style="display:none">My brain is too fried to think, and a picture is worth a thousand words so..<br><br>Let me open up by showing an accurate depiction of Robin Hobb and her characters..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921740ra/24556556.gif" width="500" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yep looks accurate enough to me.. and I thought she was mean to my babies in Farseer :') This series was borderline sadist towards those precious children.. Shall we continue?<br><br>When we finally learned the full extent of the flashbacks despite all the previous not-so-subtle hints..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556503.gif" width="317" height="174" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>when THAT scene happened..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556504.gif" width="410" height="203" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All the other near-hits..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556505.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there is the light at the end of the tunnel, when you see all the wonderful marvelous character development and how characters you started off hating with a raging fire ended being some of your favorites, but also the exact opposite can also happen, and that just proves how masterful Robin Hobb is in creating those realistic yet highly flawed personalities. I mentioned how we see immense growth throughout the series yet it all felt as a part of a natural course and none of it really felt forced in any way shape or form.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921210ra/24556506.gif" width="245" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*wipes brow* those books people, everyone should pick up Robin Hobb especially if you are like me who inhales dragons and exhales magic. <br><b>And no, it's NOT ok to skip Farseer and just start with this trilogy, or at least do it at your own risk knowing that you'll only have half the experience, an awesome experience for sure, but a truncated one nonetheless because:</b><br> A. you'll miss you on Fitz and the Fool and Burrich and Patience and Kettricken and all the merry band in the Six Duchies, despite it being majorly flawed pace-wise with a very rushed ending, if you looked at it as a part of a gigantic series you won't even feel disappointed by the super slow burn, it'll make the experience richer and more vivid every time you dive into one of her masterpieces. I cannot in good conscience say that I loved the characters in Liveships Traders or the plot more that the ones in Farseer, the only superiority I saw was in the structure of Liveships Traders and the feeling that Robin Hobb was more at ease with her world and prose that she didn't feel she needed to go on and on about useless details or insignificant happenings or just wandering around in the forest. The multiple POV certainly helps, but aside from that I equally love both trilogies when it comes to the things that matters (characteeeeeerrrrrrrrrss)<br><br>B. I gotta be honest, I saw fanart that kinda hinted at a big reveal in this trilogy that wasn't even revealed but was heavily alluded to, and you wouldn't even understand how big it is without reading the first trilogy, but OH MY GOD! I was literally screaming everytime a clue was dropped, ahhh just the way she wove all the storylines and how they come together EEEEPPP *hugs book*.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511921511ra/24556537.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now I CANNOT wait to start The Tawny Man trilogy, by far the most acclaimed trilogy in the Realm of the Elderlings *heart eyes*<br>I'm thinking though of taking a Hobb-Holiday because my heart has been through the ringer and I need me some shameless fluff.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7571545817917440774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2395066323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2395066323" />
    <a title="Victoria Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4478323-victoria-rose"><img alt="Victoria Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589799710p2/4478323.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2395066323?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Rose" href="/user/show/4478323-victoria-rose">Victoria Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008117474" href="/book/show/25985881-ship-of-destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=badass-ladies">badass-ladies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478323-victoria-rose?shelf=maritime">maritime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2395066323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7122472904714591786">I finished this on a short holiday with a good friend who I warned well in advance: "If I get a bit teary, I'm fine, it's just a really good book." He shook his head at me but accepted it, which was great because later when I got a bit teary he laughed it off as I crumpled in on myself. <br/><br/>Lord help me, Robin Hobb (as I think I've mentioned before) destroys me. In this final volume, all the individual storylines come together, situations come to wonderful, terrible climaxes, and readers everywhere </span>
  <span id="freeText7122472904714591786" style="display:none">I finished this on a short holiday with a good friend who I warned well in advance: "If I get a bit teary, I'm fine, it's just a really good book." He shook his head at me but accepted it, which was great because later when I got a bit teary he laughed it off as I crumpled in on myself. <br><br>Lord help me, Robin Hobb (as I think I've mentioned before) destroys me. In this final volume, all the individual storylines come together, situations come to wonderful, terrible climaxes, and readers everywhere collapse from excitement and emotional exhaustion. <br><br><b>1) Characterisation.</b> Hobb's characterisation is incredible. In-cred-i-ble. My least favourite character in the first instalment developed to such an extent that in this volume I wished I could be more like her. Other characters have changed so much in such amazing ways over the course of the trilogy that I was simply left in awe of their journeys. <br><br><b>2) Wisdom.</b> Why do people read self help books when books like this exist?<br><br><i>"Silencing memories does not make them stop existing. Events cannot be undone by forgetting them."</i><br><br><i>"When you fear to fail, you fear something that has not happened yet."</i><br><br><i>"Be content with your own life, my friend, and live it well. Let others decide for themselves what path they will follow."</i><br><br><i>"Who loves you or who you love is not as significant as who you are. Too many folk, women and men, love the person they wish to be, as if by loving that person, or being loved by that person, they could attain the importance they long for."</i><br><br><b>3) World building.</b> More specifically, the intricate world building not just in this specific area of the Realm of the Elderlings universe, but in previous areas too. The Six Duchies! The Farseers! THE MOMENT WHEN I REALISED A HUGE THING! God damn, that moment is going to be one I wish I could relive for ever and ever. The aforementioned friend I was travelling with had to sit patiently while I explained EVERYTHING. <i>
  <b>My soul left my body.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529553499ra/25828562.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4) The climax.</b> Oh, the ending is so good. So good. I was expecting to have my heart torn out, but it was torn out in a slightly different manner from what I was expecting. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[While the ending of the Farseer trilogy had me weeping for Verity and poor Fitz, the happy ending here made me cry simply because it was so lovely. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, the 'final battle' was everything I wanted. I'm not sure I've ever felt so satisfied. <br><br>In short: <br><br>I'm going straight onto the Tawny Man trilogy. Wish me luck.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7122472904714591786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1443041534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1443041534" />
    <a title="Petra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9654275-petra"><img alt="Petra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435928204p2/9654275.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1443041534?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra" href="/user/show/9654275-petra">Petra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780006498872" href="/book/show/395953.Ship_of_Destiny">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9654275-petra?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9654275-petra?shelf=sexual-assault-abuse">sexual-assault-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9654275-petra?shelf=multi-pov">multi-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9654275-petra?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9654275-petra?shelf=romantic-has-romance">romantic-has-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443041534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16394420908793329059">A fine, although a bit rushed finish to a remarkable fantasy trilogy.<br/><br/>The character development is still strong. I was especially pleased to see well-written female protagonists of all ages. However, because their world is very patriarchal, women do not have it easy and this book in particular goes to some dark places.<br/><br/>It includes a brutal rape of my favourite character by another major character. What made it even more heartbreaking is that no one believed her. From that point on in the book I ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16394420908793329059" style="display:none">A fine, although a bit rushed finish to a remarkable fantasy trilogy.<br /><br />The character development is still strong. I was especially pleased to see well-written female protagonists of all ages. However, because their world is very patriarchal, women do not have it easy and this book in particular goes to some dark places.<br /><br />It includes a brutal rape of my favourite character by another major character. What made it even more heartbreaking is that no one believed her. From that point on in the book I had to force myself to finish it and I managed to. But the ending wasn't satisfying. It felt rushed and sloppy and out of character, especially for my aforementioned favourite who abandones her lifelong ambition in favor of marrying and standing by her man, the idea of which she abhorred in previous novels.<br /><br />But the ending really doesn't do justice to this terrific series. Overall, these novels are certainly one of the best works of fantasy that I have read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16394420908793329059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Mvx1Hv1xaDELKjzSEMytkeU+Hzp450fhYuT+1y/qD3M2moSzIgQAMbzRdgkp0fDOM/pDnG3Ehi573Q6YKQ6q5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SGM9Q3npjZV2rv3Jo5IpQ1mwfWQgYRd9Jku4XDNTav9MBczuppzllcFVtxKaj3Qcj3QhwjVC1rI/ckgTNbfPag==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1397885202p3/25307.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">Robin Hobb
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
80,262
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11236608720526468678">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText11236608720526468678" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11236608720526468678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
